2. Create/switch a team to closed without COS — should be blocked

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:29:20]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Base directory for this skill: /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/plugins/emasoft-pr-checking-plugin/skills/pr-review  

# PR Review Pipeline  

## Overview  

Three-phase PR review that catches what standard code audits miss. Spawns specialized agents  
in sequence: correctness swarm, claim verification, skeptical review — then merges findings.  

## Prerequisites  

- `gh` CLI installed and authenticated (for `gh pr view`, `gh pr diff`)  
- The PR must exist on GitHub (need PR number or branch name)  
- `docs_dev/` directory must exist for report output  
- The merge script at `$CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT/scripts/epcp-merge-reports.sh` must be executable  

## Use when  

- Before pushing a PR to an upstream repository  
- After completing a feature branch and wanting a pre-merge quality gate  
- When asked to "review the PR", "check the PR", "audit the PR", or "pre-merge review"  
- After a swarm of code audit agents has already run (this catches what they miss)  

## Why this exists  

In a real incident, 20+ specialized audit agents checked a 40-file PR and found zero issues.  
A single external reviewer then immediately found 3 real bugs — including a function that  
claimed to populate 4 fields but actually populated zero of them. The audit swarm checked  
code correctness per-file; the reviewer checked claims against reality.  

This pipeline automates the three complementary review perspectives needed to catch 100% of  
issues:  

| Phase | Agent | What it catches | Analogy |  
|-------|-------|-----------------|---------|  
| 1 | Code Correctness (swarm) | Per-file bugs, type errors, security | Microscope |  
| 2 | Claim Verification (single) | PR description lies, missing implementations | Fact-checker |  
| 3 | Skeptical Review (single) | UX concerns, cross-file issues, design judgment | Telescope |  

## Protocol  

### Prerequisites  

Before starting, gather:  
1. The PR number (or branch name)  
2. The PR description text  
3. The list of changed files grouped by domain  

### Phase 1: Code Correctness Swarm  

Spawn **one `epcp-code-correctness-agent` per domain** in parallel.  

Group changed files by domain. Common domain splits:  

| Domain | File patterns |  
|--------|--------------|  
| shell-scripts | `*.sh`, `install-*.sh`, `update-*.sh` |  
| agent-registry | `lib/agent-registry.ts`, `types/agent.ts` |  
| messaging | `lib/messageQueue.ts`, `app/api/messages/**` |  
| terminal | `hooks/useTerminal.ts`, `components/TerminalView.tsx` |  
| ui-components | `components/*.tsx`, `app/page.tsx` |  
| api-routes | `app/api/**/*.ts` |  
| memory | `lib/consolidate.ts`, `lib/cozo-*.ts` |  
| docs | `docs/**`, `README.md` |  
| tests | `tests/**` |  
| config | `package.json`, `version.json`, `*.config.*` |  

**Spawning pattern:**  

```
For each domain with changed files:
  Task(
    subagent_type: "epcp-code-correctness-agent",
    prompt: """
      DOMAIN: {domain_name}
      FILES: {file_list}
      REPORT_PATH: docs_dev/epcp-correctness-{domain_name}.md

      Audit these files for code correctness. Read every file complet

... [8306 more chars truncated]

</div>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.

    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'

    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {

    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)

    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:35:56]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    32→    const team = await createTeam({ name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [], type, chiefOfStaffId }, managerId, agentNames)  
    33→    return NextResponse.json({ team }, { status: 201 })  
    34→  } catch (error) {  
    35→    // TeamValidationException carries the correct HTTP status code from business rule validation  
    36→    if (error instanceof TeamValidationException) {  
    37→      return NextResponse.json({ error: error.message }, { status: error.code })  
    38→    }  
    39→    console.error('Failed to create team:', error)

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale entries to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    if (cache.size > 200) {  
    47→      const now = Date.now()  
    48→      for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    49→        if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    50→      }  
    51  

... [286 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * AMP v1 Route Endpoint  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/v1/route  
     5→ *  
     6→ * Routes a message to the recipient agent within the local mesh network.  
     7→ * This is the primary message-sending endpoint for AMP providers.  
     8→ *  
     9→ * Authentication:  
    10→ *   - Bearer token (API key) for direct agent requests  
    11→ *   - X-Forwarded-From header for mesh-forwarded requests from known hosts  
    12→ *  
    13→ * Delivery methods:  
    14→ *   1. Local delivery — file system inbox + tmux notification (agent on this host)  
    15→ *   2. Mesh forwarding — HTTP POST to peer host's /api/v1/route (agent on another host)  
    16→ *   3. Relay queue — store-and-forward when recipient is offline or unreachable  
    17→ *  
    18→ * External providers (e.g. crabmail.ai) are rejected with 422 — clients must  
    19→ * send directly to the external provider using its route_url from registration.  
    20→ *  
    21→ * Resolution flow:  
    22→ *   1. Mesh-forwarded request? → local-only lookup (loop guard: never re-forward)  
    23→ *   2. Explicit remote host in address? → trust it, forward directly  
    24→ *   3. Otherwise? → checkMeshAgentExists (local first, then all peers)  
    25→ *   4. Resolved remote? → forwardToHost() → queue on failure  
    26→ *   5. Resolved local? → inbox write + tmux notification  
    27→ *   6. Not found anywhere? → inbox write + relay queue  
    28→ */  
    29→  
    30→import crypto from 'crypto'  
    31→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
    32→import { authenticateRequest } from '@/lib/amp-auth'  
    33→import { loadKeyPair, verifySignature } from '@/lib/amp-keys'  
    34→import { queueMessage } from '@/lib/amp-relay'  
    35→import { deliver } from '@/lib/message-delivery'  
    36→import { getAgent, getAgentByName, checkMeshAgentExists } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
    37→import { resolveAgentIdentifier } from '@/lib/messageQueue'  
    38→import { getSelfHostId, getHostById, isSelf, getOrganization } from '@/l  

... [4622 more chars truncated]

     5→ * Web UI endpoints (/api/messages POST, /api/agents/[id]/messages POST, etc.) call

    34→  }

    26→I gave an AI agent a real task — not autocomplete, a real engineering problem. It checked the code, read the logs, queried the database, and came back with the answer. That was the moment. *This thing can actually work.*  
    27→  
    28→Within a week I was running 35 agents across terminals. They were productive, but they couldn't talk to each other. I became the human message bus — copying context from one terminal, pasting into another. I was the bottleneck in my own AI team.  
    29→  
    30→**So I built AI Maestro** — one dashboard to see every agent, on every machine, with persistent memory and direct agent-to-agent communication. Today I run 80+ agents across multiple computers, building real companies with them every day.

     1→# Team Governance — Design Rules & Requirements  
     2→  
     3→**Version:** 1.0  
     4→**Date:** 2026-02-16  
     5→**Branch:** `feature/team-governance`  
     6→**Source:** Extracted from user instructions, audit reports, and logical inference  
     7→  
     8→---  
     9→  
    10→## Overview  
    11→  
    12→AI Maestro implements a team governance model with three roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff, Normal), two team types (open, closed), messaging isolation for closed teams, and a transfer request workflow for moving agents between closed teams. This document captures all requirements and rules that the implementation must enforce.  
    13→  
    14→---  
    15→  
    16→## R1. Team Type Rules  
    17→  
    18→| ID | Rule | Source |  
    19→|----|------|--------|  
    20→| R1.1 | Teams have exactly two types: `open` and `closed` | Explicit |  
    21→| R1.2 | New teams are created as `open` by default | Explicit |  
    22→| R1.3 | Changing a team to `closed` **REQUIRES** designating a Chief-of-Staff (COS) | Explicit |  
    23→| R1.4 | A closed team **MUST** always have a COS — this is an invariant that must never be violated | Explicit |  
    24→| R1.5 | Removing COS from a closed team **immediately** downgrades it to `open` | Explicit |  
    25→| R1.6 | To re-close a downgraded team, a MANAGER or COS must edit it and assign a new COS | Explicit |  
    26→| R1.7 | `TeamType` must be validated at the API layer — only `'open'` or `'closed'` accepted, anything else is rejected | Implicit (audit gap) |  
    27→| R1.8 | COS can only be set on a team of type `closed` — setting COS on an open team is invalid unless the operation also changes the type to closed | Implicit (logical consequence of R1.3) |  
    28→  
    29→**Rationale:** The COS is the gatekeeper of a closed team. Without a COS, the team cannot function as closed because no one can authorize external communication or manage membership.  
    30→  
    31→---  
    32→  
    33→## R2. Team Name Rules  
    34→  
    35→| ID | Rule | Source |  
  

... [10153 more chars truncated]

**Result:**

     1→#!/bin/bash  
     2→# AI Maestro - Version Bump Script  
     3→# Centralizes version management across all files  
     4→#  
     5→# Usage:  
     6→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
     7→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
     8→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0  
     9→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh 0.18.0   # Set specific version  
    10→  
    11→set -e  
    12→  
    13→# Colors  
    14→RED='\033[0;31m'  
    15→GREEN='\033[0;32m'  
    16→YELLOW='\033[1;33m'  
    17→CYAN='\033[0;36m'  
    18→NC='\033[0m'  
    19→  
    20→# Get script directory and project root  
    21→SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"  
    22→PROJECT_ROOT="$(dirname "$SCRIPT_DIR")"  
    23→  
    24→# Read current version from version.json  
    25→VERSION_FILE="$PROJECT_ROOT/version.json"  
    26→if [ ! -f "$VERSION_FILE" ]; then  
    27→    echo -e "${RED}Error: version.json not found${NC}"  
    28→    exit 1  
    29→fi  
    30→  
    31→CURRENT_VERSION=$(grep -o '"version": *"[^"]*"' "$VERSION_FILE" | cut -d'"' -f4)  
    32→echo -e "${CYAN}Current version: ${CURRENT_VERSION}${NC}"  
    33→  
    34→# Parse current version  
    35→IFS='.' read -r MAJOR MINOR PATCH <<< "$CURRENT_VERSION"  
    36→  
    37→# Determine new version  
    38→case "$1" in  
    39→    patch)  
    40→        PATCH=$((PATCH + 1))  
    41→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    42→        ;;  
    43→    minor)  
    44→        MINOR=$((MINOR + 1))  
    45→        PATCH=0  
    46→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    47→        ;;  
    48→    major)  
    49→        MAJOR=$((MAJOR + 1))  
    50→        MINOR=0  
    51→        PATCH=0  
    52→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    53→        ;;  
    54→    "")  
    55→        echo ""  
    56→        echo "Usage: $0 <patch|minor|major|version>"  
    57→        echo ""  
    58→        echo "Examples:"  
    59→        echo "  $0 patch    # ${CURRENT_VERSION} -> ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.$((PATCH + 1  

... [4706 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→

    11→  
    12→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    13→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    14→  recipientAgentId: string

    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→  
    46→  // Load team membership for both parties

   116→/** Check if agentId is chief-of-staff in any closed team */  
   117→export function isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(agentId: string): boolean {  
   118→  const teams = loadTeams()  
   119→  return teams.some(  
   120→    (team) => team.type === 'closed' && team.chiefOfStaffId === agentId  
   121→  )  
   122→}  
   123→  
   124→/** Get the first closed team where agentId is a member (normal agents belong to at most one) */  
   125→export function getClosedTeamForAgent(agentId: string): Team | null {  
   126→  const teams = loadTeams()  
   127→  return (  
   128→    teams.find(  
   129→      (team) => team.type === 'closed' && team.agentIds.includes(agentId)  
   130→    ) || null  
   131→  )  
   132→}  
   133→  
   134→/** Get all closed teams where agentId is a member (MANAGER/COS can be in multiple) */  
   135→export function getClosedTeamsForAgent(agentId: string): Team[] {  
   136→  const teams = loadTeams()  
   137→  return teams.filter(  
   138→    (team) => team.type === 'closed' && team.agentIds.includes(agentId)  
   139→  )  
   140→}

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [149 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:32:59]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good, `globals: true` is set, so `afterEach` is available globally. Not an issue, but it's an inconsistency - some tests import `afterEach` while others rely on the global.  

Now let me verify one more critical thing about the transfer-registry test: the fs mock structure vs the source's import style.  

The source `transfer-registry.ts` uses:  
```typescript
import { readFileSync, writeFileSync, mkdirSync, existsSync } from 'fs'
```

The test mocks:  
```typescript
vi.mock('fs', () => ({
  existsSync: vi.fn(...),
  mkdirSync: vi.fn(),
  readFileSync: vi.fn(...),
  writeFileSync: vi.fn(...),
}))
```

Named exports from `fs` map to the top-level of the mock object. This is correct for vitest. However, `os.homedir()` is used in the test helpers but the source uses `process.env.HOME`. This means the path computed in the test helper (`path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro')`) may differ from the source's path (`path.join(process.env.HOME || '~', '.aimaestro')`). If `process.env.HOME` equals `os.homedir()` (which it does on macOS/Linux), this works. But it's fragile.  

Let me also check for the `readFileSync` encoding parameter issue: the source passes `'utf-8'` but the mock doesn't check for it.  

Now let me check the mock consistency for governance.test.ts - the fs mock uses `default.*`:  

Governance.ts uses `import fs from 'fs'` (default import), and the test mocks `fs` as `{ default: { existsSync, ... } }`. With vitest, when you `import fs from 'fs'`, vitest maps the default import to the `default` property of the mock. This is correct.  

Team-registry.ts also uses `import fs from 'fs'`, and team-registry.test.ts mocks `fs` as `{ default: { existsSync, ... } }`. This is correct.  

Document-api.test.ts mocks `fs` as `{ default: { existsSync, ... } }`. The document-registry.ts uses `import fs from 'fs'`. The API routes call into both `team-registry` and `document-registry`, both using default imports. This is correct.  

Now let me check the `isChiefOfStaffAnywhere` test more carefully. The governance.test.ts test at line 203-231 mocks `loadTeams` to return teams where the COS is in both open and closed teams. The real `isChiefOfStaffAnywhere` checks `team.type === 'closed'`. The test checks that the function returns true for 'agent-cos-1', who is COS on both an open team and a closed team. This is correct -- but the test only checks `isChiefOfStaffAnywhere` for the COS role -- it does NOT test the negative case where an agent is COS of only open teams (should return false). That's a coverage gap.  

Let me now check the `message-filter.test.ts` more carefully. The mock for `getClosedTeamsForAgent` returns the team objects. Looking at the source, `checkMessageAllowed` accesses `team.agentIds` (line 73) and `team.id` (line 86) and `team.chiefOfStaffId` (line 92). The mock team objects from `makeClosedTeam` include all these fields. Good.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:33:18]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good, `afterEach` is used here but relies on vitest globals. Not a bug, just inconsistent style.  

Now I have enough information to write the comprehensive report. Let me trace through a few final things.  

**transfer-registry.test.ts mock issue with `crypto`:**  
The source uses `import { randomUUID } from 'crypto'` but the test mocks `crypto` module:  
```typescript
vi.mock('crypto', () => ({
  randomUUID: vi.fn(() => `uuid-${++uuidCounter}`),
}))
```
This is the correct approach for named imports.  

**team-api.test.ts - missing mocks for transitive dependencies:**  
The `PUT` and `GET` routes for `/api/teams/[id]` call `checkTeamAccess` from `@/lib/team-acl`. This function calls `getTeam()` and `isManager()`. Since `getTeam()` calls `loadTeams()` which uses the mocked `fs`, and `isManager()` calls `loadGovernance()` which also uses the mocked `fs`, everything works through the same mock. The tests don't send `X-Agent-Id` header, so `checkTeamAccess` gets `undefined` for `requestingAgentId` and returns `{ allowed: true }` immediately (web UI path). This is correct but means the **ACL is never tested** through the API tests.  

**team-api.test.ts - `createTeam` signature mismatch:**  
The test calls `createTeam({ name: 'Team A', agentIds: [] })` directly (line 80), but the real `createTeam` accepts optional `managerId` and `reservedNames` params. The test only passes the first arg, so `managerId` and `reservedNames` default to `undefined`. The API route passes them, but the test's direct call doesn't. This means the test's direct `createTeam` calls DON'T go through the validation that the API route would trigger with `loadAgents()` and `getManagerId()`. Not a bug per se, but the tests bypass some validation.  

Let me write the report now.

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]  

</details>

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  

</details>

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { verifyPassword, setManager, removeManager, loadGovernance } from '@/lib/governance'

     5→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     6→  try {  
     7→    const body = await request.json()  
     8→    const { agentId, password } = body  
     9→  
    10→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string') {  
    11→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Governance password is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    12→    }  
    13→  
    14→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    15→    if (!config.passwordHash) {  
    16→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Governance password not set. Set a password first via POST /api/governance/password' }, { status: 400 })  
    17→    }  
    18→  
    19→    if (!verifyPassword(password)) {  
    20→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid governance password' }, { status: 401 })  
    21→    }  
    22→  
    23→    if (agentId === null) {  
    24→      await removeManager()  
    25→      return NextResponse.json({ success: true, managerId: null })  
    26→    }  
    27→  
    28→    if (typeof agentId !== 'string' || !agentId.trim()) {  
    29→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId must be a non-empty string or null' }, { status: 400 })  
    30→    }  
    31→  
    32→    // Verify agent exists  
    33→    const agent = getAgent(agentId)  
    34→    if (!agent) {  
    35→      return NextResponse.json({ error: `Agent '${agentId}' not found` }, { status: 404 })  
    36→    }  
    37→  
    38→    await setManager(agentId)  
    39→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true, managerId: agentId, managerName: agent.name || agent.alias })  
    40→  } catch (error) {  
    41→    console.error('Failed to set manager:', error)  
    42→    return NextResponse.json(  
    43→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set manager' },  
    44→      { status: 500 }

     2→import { loadGovernance, setPassword, verifyPassword } from '@/lib/governance'  
     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    await setPassword(password)  
    23→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    24→  } catch (error) {  
    25→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    26→    return NextResponse.json(  
    27→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    28→      { status: 500 }  
    29→    )  
    30→  }

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale entries to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    if (cache.size > 200) {  
    47→      const now = Date.now()  
    48→      for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    49→        if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    50→      }  
    51  

... [286 more chars truncated]

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager, isChiefOfStaffAnywhere, getClosedTeamsForAgent } from './governance'  
    11→  
    12→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    13→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    14→  recipientAgentId: string  
    15→  isMeshForwarded?: boolean  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→  
    46→  // Load team membership for both parties  

... [2677 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    31→    fetchTeam().finally(() => setLoading(false))  
    32→  }, [teamId, fetchTeam])  
    33→  ```  
    34→- **Fix:** Change `useTeam` to initialize `loading` as `true` when `teamId` is provided: `const [loading, setLoading] = useState(!!teamId)`. Or alternatively, in `[id]/page.tsx`, change the guard to also check if `team === null && !error` to distinguish "loading" from "not found".

    15→- **Description:** The `teamId` parameter is interpolated directly into a file path without any sanitization. The `getTeam(id)` check (which loads from the teams registry, not the filesystem) would return `null` and the route would 404 before reaching `loadTasks`/`saveTasks` — **BUT** this safety depends entirely on `getTeam` rejecting the ID. If team IDs were ever user-controlled strings (not UUIDs), or if a code path bypassed the `getTeam` check, files outside the teams directory could be read or written.

    21→  }  
    22→  ```  
    23→  The API routes do call `getTeam(id)` first (which validates the ID exists as a UUID in teams.json), so this is currently protected by defense-in-depth. However, the `tasksFilePath` function itself is unsafe and could be misused by future callers.  
    24→- **Fix:** Validate that `teamId` matches a UUID pattern (`/^[0-9a-f-]{36}$/i`) in `tasksFilePath`, or use `path.basename()` to strip directory traversal characters: `path.join(TEAMS_DIR, \`tasks-${pat

    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** In `removeAgentFromTeam`, the code first computes `updatedAgentIds` by filtering out `targetAgentId` (line 202), then checks if the agent is the COS (line 205). The guard returns an error, which is correct, but only AFTER the filter operation has already been computed. While the filtered array is not sent to the server in that case (the early return prevents it), the real problem is that the guard should run BEFORE computing the update to make the intent clear and avoid future refactoring bugs. More critically, if someone later adds optimistic state updates using `updatedAgentIds` before the guard check, the COS would be incorrectly removed from the local state.  
    16→  
    17→  **However**, the more pressing issue is the ordering logic itself. The guard at line 205 checks `team.chiefOfStaffId === targetAgentId`, but this check happens after the network fetch of the team (line 197). Between the fetch and the PUT, the COS could have changed server-side (TOCTOU race). The server enforces this too (comment says so), so the functional impact is low, but the client-side guard gives a false sense of security.  
    18→- **Evidence:**  
    19→  ```typescript  
    20→  // Line 202: filter runs first  
    21→  const updatedAgentIds = team.agentIds.filter((id: string) => id !== targetAgentId)  
    22→  
    23→  // Line 205-207: guard runs second

    20→function ensureTeamsDir() {

    25→  
    26→function pruneOldEnded(meetings: Meeting[]): Meeting[] {  
    27→  const cutoff = Date.now() - PRUNE_DAYS * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000  
    28→  return meetings.filter(m => {  
    29→    if (m.status !== 'ended' || !m.endedAt) return true  
    30→    return new Date(m.endedAt).getTime() > cutoff  
    31→  })  
    32→}  
    33→  
    34→export function loadMeetings(): Meeting[] {  
    35→  try {  
    36→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    37→    if (!fs.existsSync(MEETINGS_FILE)) {  
    38→      return []  
    39→    }  
    40→    const data = fs.readFileSync(MEETINGS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    41→    const parsed: MeetingsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    42→    const meetings = Array.isArray(parsed.meetings) ? parsed.meetings : []  
    43→    // Auto-prune old ended meetings  
    44→    const pruned = pruneOldEnded(meetings)  
    45→    if (pruned.length !== meetings.length) {  
    46→      saveMeetings(pruned)  
    47→    }  
    48→    return pruned  
    49→  } catch (error) {  
    50→    console.error('Failed to load meetings:', error)  
    51→    return []  
    52→  }  
    53→}

    55→function meetingReducer(state: TeamMeetingState, action: TeamMeetingAction): TeamMeetingState {  
    56→  switch (action.type) {  
    57→    case 'SELECT_AGENT':  
    58→      if (state.phase === 'active') {  
    59→        return {  
    60→          ...state,  
    61→          selectedAgentIds: state.selectedAgentIds.includes(action.agentId)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:33:18]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The RESTORE_MEETING handler in the reducer (lines 165-181) doesn't set `notifyAmp`. But since the spread `...state` preserves the current value and the initial state is `false`, this just means restored meetings don't change the notifyAmp flag, which is reasonable. The RESTORE_MEETING does set `rightPanelOpen: false`, `rightPanelTab: 'tasks'`, and `kanbanOpen: false`, so it resets transient UI state. The notifyAmp is also transient and it defaults to false, so this is fine.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:33:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I notice `DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG` is a const defined in the types file but it's mutable -- fields like `passwordHash` and `managerId` are assigned directly in `governance.ts` (e.g., `config.passwordHash = ...`). Since `loadGovernance` returns a spread copy (`{ ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }`), this is safe. But the `saveGovernance(DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG)` on line 36 passes the original constant directly -- this is fine since `saveGovernance` only serializes it with JSON.stringify, it doesn't mutate it.

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.

    20→  reason?: string

    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation

    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted

    19→  if (!existsSync(AI_MAESTRO_DIR)) {  
    20→    mkdirSync(AI_MAESTRO_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    21→  }  
    22→}  
    23→  
    24→/** Load all transfer requests from disk */

    32→    const data: TransfersFile = JSON.parse(raw)  
    33→    return data.requests || []  
    34→  } catch {  
    35→    return []  
    36→  }  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/** Save transfer requests to disk */  
    40→function saveTransfers(requests: TransferRequest[]): void {  
    41→  ensureDir()  
    42→  const data: TransfersFile = { version: 1, requests }  
    43→  writeFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, JSON.stringify(data, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    44→}

Looking at the code again -- `setPassword` (line 61-68), `setManager` (line 86-92), `removeManager` (line 95-101) all call `saveGovernance()` but never check its boolean return. If the save fails, the operation silently appears to succeed.  

Let me check if there could be a race in `loadTeams()` migration.  

The `loadTeams()` function at line 194-221 calls `saveTeams(teams)` inside a migration path, but `loadTeams()` itself is NOT wrapped in a lock. If two requests call `loadTeams()` simultaneously, both might see `needsSave = true` and both write -- this is benign (same data), but it's a potential issue if either write partially fails.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:32:38]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I see a type safety issue at line 283: `updates as Record<string, unknown>` is a type assertion cast that bypasses TypeScript's type checking. The `validateTeamMutation` function expects specific properties (`name`, `type`, `chiefOfStaffId`, `agentIds`), but this cast silently allows any property. However, this is harmless in practice since `validateTeamMutation` only accesses the properties it expects.  

Now let me check the `cleanupOldTransfers` ISO date comparison.  

Looking at line 125 of transfer-registry.ts:  
```typescript
return (r.resolvedAt || r.createdAt) > cutoffStr
```

ISO 8601 date strings ARE lexicographically sortable, so this comparison is valid.  

Let me check if `message-send.ts` has a potential issue with the conditional message filter check.  

At line 153 in message-send.ts:  
```typescript
if (fromAgent?.agentId && toResolved.agentId) {
```

If `toResolved.agentId` is an empty string (line 146), this condition is `false`, and the governance filter is SKIPPED. This means if the recipient cannot be resolved to a UUID, governance filtering is entirely bypassed for `sendFromUI`.  

Let me also verify the `\w` in the regex at line 92 of team-registry.ts.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:32:44]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

`\w` matches `[a-zA-Z0-9_]`, but it also matches Unicode word characters in some engines. In the V8 engine (Node.js), `\w` only matches `[a-zA-Z0-9_]` without the Unicode flag, so this is fine.  

Now I have all the information I need. Let me write the report.

     1→'use client'

     4→import type { Team } from '@/types/team'

     6→interface UseTeamResult {  
     7→  team: Team | null  
     8→  loading: boolean

    14→export function useTeam(teamId: string | null): UseTeamResult {  
    15→  const [team, setTeam] = useState<Team | null>(null)  
    16→  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false)  
    17→  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null)

    20→    if (!teamId) return

    22→      const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`)  
    23→      if (!res.ok) throw new Error('Failed to fetch team')  
    24→      const data = await res.json()  
    25→      setTeam(data.team || null)  
    26→      setError(null)  
    27→    } catch (err) {  
    28→      setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to fetch team')  
    29→    }  
    30→  }, [teamId])  
    31→  
    32→  // Initial fetch

    34→    if (!teamId) {  
    35→      setTeam(null)  
    36→      return  
    37→    }  
    38→    setLoading(true)  
    39→    fetchTeam().finally(() => setLoading(false))  
    40→  }, [teamId, fetchTeam])  
    41→  
    42→  const updateTeam = useCallback(async (updates: { name?: string; description?: string; agentIds?: string[]; instructions?: string }) => {  
    43→    if (!teamId) return  
    44→    // Optimistic update  
    45→    setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)  
    46→    const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`, {  
    47→      method: 'PUT',  
    48→      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },  
    49→      body: JSON.stringify({ ...updates, lastActivityAt: n

     1→'use client'

     6→import { useHosts } from './useHosts'  
     7→import { cacheRemoteAgents, getCachedAgents } from '@/lib/agent-cache'  
     8→  
     9→const REFRESH_INTERVAL = 10000 // 10 seconds  
    10→const SELF_FETCH_TIMEOUT = 8000 // 8 seconds for self host (tmux queries can be slow)  
    11→const PEER_FETCH_TIMEOUT = 3000 // 3 seconds for peer hosts (fail fast, use cache)  
    12→  
    13→/**  
    14→ * Check if a host URL points to localhost (the machine running this dashboard)  
    15→ * Used client-side since os.hostname() isn't available in browser  
    16→ */  
    17→function isLocalhostUrl(url: string | undefined): boolean {  
    18→  if (!url) return true  
    19→  const lowered = url.toLowerCase()  
    20→  return lowered.includes('localhost') || lowered.includes('127.0.0.1')  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Aggregated stats across all hosts  
    25→ */  
    26→interface AggregatedStats {  
    27→  total: number  
    28→  online: number  
    29→  offline: number  
    30→  orphans: number  
    31→  newlyRegistered: number  
    32→  cached: number // Number of agents loaded from cache  
    33→}  
    34→  
    35→/**  
    36→ * Host fetch result  
    37→ */  
    38→interface HostFetchResult {  
    39→  hostId: string  
    40→  success: boolean  
    41→  response?: AgentsApiResponse  
    42→  error?: Error  
    43→  fromCache?: boolean  
    44→}  
    45→  
    46→/**  
    47→ * Fetch agents from a specific host  
    48→ */  
    49→async function fetchHostAgents(host: Host): Promise<HostFetchResult> {  
    50→  const isSelf = isLocalhostUrl(host.url)  
    51→  const baseUrl = isSelf ? '' : host.url  
    52→  const timeout = isSelf ? SELF_FETCH_TIMEOUT : PEER_FETCH_TIMEOUT  
    53→

   101→/**  
   102→ * Compute tmux session name from agent name and session index  
   103→ * Examples:  
   104→ *   ("website", 0) → "website"  
   105→ *   ("website", 1) → "website_1"  
   106→ *   ("23blocks-apps-backend", 0) → "23blocks-apps-backend"  
   107→ *   ("23blocks-apps-backend", 2) → "23blocks-apps-backend_2"  
   108→ */  
   109→export function computeSessionName(agentName: string, index: number): string {  
   110→  return index === 0 ? agentName : `${agentName}_${index}`  
   111→}  
   112→  
   113→/**  
   114→ * Derive display info from agent name for UI hierarchy  
   115→ * Splits on hyphens to create tags + shortName  
   116→ * Examples:  
   117→ *   "website" → { tags: [], shortName: "website" }  
   118→ *   "23blocks-apps-website" → { tags: ["23blocks", "apps"], shortName: "website" }  
   119→ */  
   120→export function parseNameForDisplay(name: string): { tags: string[]; shortName: string } {  
   121→  const segments = name.split(/-/).filter(s => s.length > 0)  
   122→  if (segments.length === 1) {  
   123→    return { tags: [], shortName: segments[0] }  
   124→  }  
   125→  return {  
   126→    tags: segments.slice(0, -1),  
   127→    shortName: segments[segments.length - 1]  
   128→  }  
   129→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 20:31:48]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

CONFIRMED: `loading` starts as `false` in `useTeam` (line 16). The `useEffect` on line 33-40 sets `loading` to `true` in the effect body (not synchronously during render), so there is a race: on the very first render, `loading=false` and `team=null`, which means the condition `if (loading || !team)` at line 31 of `[id]/page.tsx` evaluates to `true` (because `!team`), and the displayed message is `'Team not found'` (because `loading` is `false`). This is a flash of incorrect "Team not found" message before the effect runs and sets `loading=true`.  

Now let me verify the `TeamOverviewSection` stale state issue -- when `team` prop changes, `name` and `description` local state won't update.  

Looking at lines 22-23 of TeamOverviewSection.tsx:  
```tsx
const [name, setName] = useState(team.name)
const [description, setDescription] = useState(team.description || '')
```

These `useState` calls use `team.name` / `team.description` as initial values only. If the parent re-renders with a new `team` prop (e.g., after an update from a different tab/user), the local `name` and `description` state will NOT update. This is a stale state bug.  

Now let me check if `validateTeamName` is missing from the dependency array anywhere or has other issues.  

Looking at the create team flow in `page.tsx`, on line 245: `if (e.key === 'Enter' && !nameValidation.error) handleCreateTeam()` -- but `handleCreateTeam` also checks `!newTeamName.trim()` on line 119. However, `handleCreateTeam` does NOT check `nameValidation.error`. So if the user types a name that passes the trim check but has a validation error, pressing Enter is correctly blocked by the onKeyDown handler (line 245), but clicking the "Create" button (line 266-268) has `disabled={!newTeamName.trim() || !!nameValidation.error}` which also correctly blocks it. The issue is that `handleCreateTeam` itself doesn't check validation, meaning any direct call to it could bypass validation. But all call sites do check, so this is a minor defensive programming issue.  

Let me also check for the unhandled promise in the async handlers.  

In `TeamOverviewSection.tsx`:  
- `handleSaveName` (line 29): async, called from `onClick` (line 68) and `onKeyDown` (line 66). No `.catch()` -- if `onUpdateTeam` rejects, this becomes an unhandled promise rejection.  
- `handleSaveDesc` (line 36): same pattern.  
- `handleRemoveAgent` (line 43): async, called from `onClick` (line 247). Same issue.  
- `handleAddAgent` (line 48): async, called from `onClick` (line 211). Same issue.  

These are all event handlers that call async functions without error handling. If the API call fails, the promise rejection is unhandled.  

Now I have enough findings. Let me write the report.  

</div>
